<p>Bank of America has formed a partnership with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a> creating a newly chartered bank <b>DOD Community Bank</b><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> ("Community Bank") providing full banking services to military personnel at 68 branches and ATM locations<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> on U.S. military installations in <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_Naval_Base" title="Guantanamo Bay Naval Base">Guantanamo Bay Naval Base</a> <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diego_Garcia" title="Diego Garcia">Diego Garcia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kwajalein_Atoll" title="Kwajalein Atoll">Kwajalein Atoll</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. Even though Bank of America operates Community Bank customer services are not interchangeable between the two financial institutions,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> meaning a Community Bank customer cannot go to a Bank of America branch and withdraw from their account and vice versa. Deposits made into checking and savings accounts are insured by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Deposit_Insurance_Corporation" title="Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation">Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation</a> up to $250,000 despite the fact that none of Community's operating branches are located within the jurisdictional borders of the United States.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Decision_not_to_finance_makers_of_military-style_guns">Decision not to finance makers of military-style guns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Decision not to finance makers of military-style guns" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In April 2018, Bank of America announced that it would stop providing financing to makers of military-style weapons such as the AR-15 rifle.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> In announcing the decision, Bank of America referenced recent mass shootings and said that it wanted to "contribute in any way we can" to reduce them.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="Return_to_expansion_.282015-present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_expansion_(2015-present)">Return to expansion (2015-present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Return to expansion (2015-present)" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In 2015, Bank of America began expanding organically, opening branches in cities where it previously did not have a retail presence. They started that year in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis%E2%80%93Saint_Paul" title="Minneapolis–Saint Paul">Minneapolis–Saint Paul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, in all cases having at least one of its <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_(banking)#United_States" title="Big Four (banking)">Big Four</a> competitors, with <a href="/wiki/Chase_Bank" title="Chase Bank">Chase Bank</a> being available in Denver and Indianapolis, while <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a> is available in Denver and the Twin Cities.<sup id="cite_ref-Pittsburgh_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pittsburgh-103">[103]</a></sup> The Twin Cities market is also the home market of <a href="/wiki/U.S._Bancorp" title="U.S. Bancorp">U.S. Bancorp</a>, the largest non-Big Four rival.
</p><p>In January 2018, Bank of America announced an organic expansion of its retail footprint into <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a> and surrounding areas, to supplement its existing commercial lending and investment businesses in the area. Before the expansion, Pittsburgh had been one of the largest US cities without a retail presence by any of the Big Four, with locally based <a href="/wiki/PNC_Financial_Services" title="PNC Financial Services">PNC Financial Services</a> (no. 6 nationally) having a commanding market share in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Pittsburgh_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pittsburgh-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The following month, Bank of America announced it would expand into Ohio across the state's three biggest cities (<a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>), which are also strongholds of Chase.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Operations" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_America_-_Near_Northeast.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Bank_of_America_-_Near_Northeast.JPG/220px-Bank_of_America_-_Near_Northeast.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3255" data-file-height="2059"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 139px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Bank_of_America_-_Near_Northeast.JPG/220px-Bank_of_America_-_Near_Northeast.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="139" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_America_-_Near_Northeast.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bank of America branch in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a></div></div></div>
<p>Bank of America generates 90% of its revenues in its domestic market. The core of Bank of America's strategy is to be the number one bank in its domestic market. It has achieved this through key acquisitions.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumer_Banking">Consumer Banking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Consumer Banking" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Consumer Banking, the largest division in the company, provides financial services to consumers and small businesses including, banking, investments and lending products including business loans, mortgages, and credit cards. It provides <a href="/wiki/Stockbroker" title="Stockbroker">stockbroker</a> services via <a href="/wiki/Merrill_Edge" title="Merrill Edge">Merrill Edge</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Electronic_trading_platform" title="Electronic trading platform">electronic trading platform</a>. The consumer banking division represented 38% of the company's total revenue in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-10K_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K-1">[1]</a></sup> The company earns revenue from interest income, service charges, and fees. The company is also a <a href="/wiki/Mortgage_servicer" title="Mortgage servicer">mortgage servicer</a>. It competes primarily with the <a href="/wiki/Retail_banking" title="Retail banking">retail banking</a> arms of America's three other megabanks: <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a>, <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a>. The Consumer Banking organization includes over 4,600 retail financial centers and approximately 15,900 <a href="/wiki/Automated_teller_machine" title="Automated teller machine">automated teller machines</a>.
</p><p>Bank of America is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Global_ATM_Alliance" title="Global ATM Alliance">Global ATM Alliance</a>, a joint venture of several major international banks that provides for reduced fees for consumers using their <a href="/wiki/Automated_teller_machine" title="Automated teller machine">ATM</a> card or <a href="/wiki/Check_card" title="Check card">check card</a> at another bank within the Global ATM Alliance when traveling internationally. This feature is restricted to withdrawals using a debit card and users are still subject to foreign currency conversion fees, credit card withdrawals are still subject to cash advance fees and foreign currency conversion fees.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_Banking">Global Banking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Global Banking" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LaurastBOAT.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/LaurastBOAT.jpg/170px-LaurastBOAT.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1895" data-file-height="2526"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 227px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/LaurastBOAT.jpg/170px-LaurastBOAT.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="227" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LaurastBOAT.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Tower_(Jacksonville)" title="Bank of America Tower (Jacksonville)">Bank of America Tower</a>, located on <a href="/wiki/Laura_Street" title="Laura Street">Laura Street</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville, Florida</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Global Banking division provides banking services, including investment banking and lending products to businesses. It includes the businesses of Global Corporate Banking, Global Commercial Banking, Business Banking, and Global Investment Banking. The division represented 22% of the company's revenue in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-10K_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K-1">[1]</a></sup></p><p>Before Bank of America's acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Merrill_Lynch" class="mw-redirect" title="Merrill Lynch">Merrill Lynch</a>, the Global Corporate and Investment Banking (GCIB) business operated as <a href="/wiki/Banc_of_America_Securities" class="mw-redirect" title="Banc of America Securities">Banc of America Securities</a> LLC. The bank's investment banking activities operate under the Merrill Lynch subsidiary and provided <a href="/wiki/Mergers_and_acquisitions" title="Mergers and acquisitions">mergers and acquisitions</a> advisory, <a href="/wiki/Underwriting" title="Underwriting">underwriting</a>, capital markets, as well as sales &amp; trading in fixed income and equities markets. Its strongest groups include <a href="/wiki/Leverage_(finance)" title="Leverage (finance)">Leveraged Finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syndicated_Loans" class="mw-redirect" title="Syndicated Loans">Syndicated Loans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mortgage-backed_security" title="Mortgage-backed security">mortgage-backed securities</a>. It also has one of the largest research teams on <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Merrill_Lynch" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of America Merrill Lynch">Bank of America Merrill Lynch</a> is headquartered in New York City.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_Wealth_and_Investment_Management">Global Wealth and Investment Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Global Wealth and Investment Management" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The Global Wealth and Investment Management (GWIM) division manages investment assets of institutions and individuals. It includes the businesses of Merrill Lynch Global Wealth Management and U.S. Trust and represented 21% of the company's total revenue in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-10K_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K-1">[1]</a></sup> It is among the 10 largest U.S. wealth managers. It has over $2.5 trillion in client balances.<sup id="cite_ref-10K_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K-1">[1]</a></sup> GWIM has five primary lines of business: Premier Banking &amp; Investments (including Bank of America Investment Services, Inc.), The Private Bank, Family Wealth Advisors, and Bank of America Specialist.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_Markets">Global Markets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Global Markets" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The Global Markets division offers services to institutional clients, including trading in <a href="/wiki/Financial_securities" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial securities">financial securities</a>. The division provides research and other services such as <a href="/wiki/Market_maker" title="Market maker">market maker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Risk_management" title="Risk management">risk management</a> using <a href="/wiki/Derivative_(finance)" title="Derivative (finance)">derivatives</a>. The division represented 19% of the company's total revenues in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-10K_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Labor">Labor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Labor" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On April 9, 2019, the company announced minimum wage will be increased beginning May 1, 2019, to $17.00 an hour until it reaches a goal of $20.00 an hour in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Offices">Offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Offices" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The Bank of America principal executive offices are located in the Bank of America Corporate Center, Charlotte, North Carolina. The skyscraper is located at 100 North Tryon Street, and stands at 871 ft (265 m), having been completed in 1992.
</p><p>In 2012, Bank of America cut ties to the <a href="/wiki/American_Legislative_Exchange_Council" title="American Legislative Exchange Council">American Legislative Exchange Council</a> (ALEC).<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="International_offices">International offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: International offices" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Bank of America's Global Corporate and Investment Banking has its U.S. headquarters in Charlotte, European headquarters in Dublin, and Asian headquarters in Hong Kong and Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_Governance">Corporate Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Corporate Governance" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">

<td>
</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Charitable_efforts">Charitable efforts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Charitable efforts" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_America_LA_Pride_2011.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Bank_of_America_LA_Pride_2011.jpg/220px-Bank_of_America_LA_Pride_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Bank_of_America_LA_Pride_2011.jpg/220px-Bank_of_America_LA_Pride_2011.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_America_LA_Pride_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bank of America volunteers at the Los Angeles LGBT pride parade in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>In 2007, the bank offered employees a $3,000 rebate for the purchase of hybrid vehicles. The company also provided a $1,000 rebate or a lower interest rate for customers whose homes qualified as energy efficient.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> In 2007, Bank of America partnered with Brighter Planet to offer an eco-friendly credit card, and later a debit card, which help build renewable energy projects with each purchase.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> In 2010, the bank completed construction of the 1 Bank of America Center in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_center_city" class="mw-redirect" title="Charlotte center city">Charlotte center city</a>. The tower, and accompanying hotel, is a <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED-certified</a> building.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p><p>Bank of America has also donated money to help health centers in Massachusetts<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> and made a $1 million donation in 2007 to help homeless shelters in Miami.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p><p>In 1998, the bank made a ten-year commitment of $350 billion to provide affordable mortgage, build affordable housing, support small business and create jobs in disadvantaged neighborhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p><p>In 2004, the bank pledged $750 million over a ten-year period for community development lending and affordable housing programs.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="CEO_pay_ratio">CEO pay ratio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: CEO pay ratio" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<p>Pursuant to Section 953(b) of the <a href="/wiki/Dodd-Frank_Wall_Street_Reform_and_Consumer_Protection_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Dodd-Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act">Dodd-Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act</a>, publicly traded companies are required to disclose (1) the median total annual compensation of all employees other than the CEO and (2) the ratio of the CEO's annual total compensation to that of the median employee.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p><p>Total 2018 compensation for <a href="/wiki/Brian_Moynihan" title="Brian Moynihan">Brian Moynihan</a>, CEO, amounted to $22,765,354, and total compensation of the median employee was determined to be $92,040. The resulting pay ratio is estimated to be 247:1.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuits">Lawsuits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Lawsuits" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>In August 2011, Bank of America was sued for $10 billion by <a href="/wiki/American_International_Group" title="American International Group">American International Group</a>. Another lawsuit filed in September 2011 pertained to $57.5 billion in <a href="/wiki/Mortgage-backed_securities" class="mw-redirect" title="Mortgage-backed securities">mortgage-backed securities</a> Bank of America sold to <a href="/wiki/Fannie_Mae" title="Fannie Mae">Fannie Mae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mac" title="Freddie Mac">Freddie Mac</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> That December, Bank of America agreed to pay $335 million to settle a federal government claim that Countrywide Financial had <a href="/wiki/Mortgage_discrimination" title="Mortgage discrimination">discriminated</a> against Hispanic and <a href="/wiki/African-American" class="mw-redirect" title="African-American">African-American</a> homebuyers from 2004 to 2008, prior to being acquired by BofA.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In September 2012, BofA settled out of court for $2.4 billion in a class action lawsuit filed by BofA shareholders who felt they were misled about the purchase of <a href="/wiki/Merrill_Lynch" class="mw-redirect" title="Merrill Lynch">Merrill Lynch</a>.
</p><p>On February 9, 2012, it was announced that the five largest mortgage servicers (Ally/GMAC, Bank of America, Citi, JPMorgan Chase, and Wells Fargo) agreed to a historic settlement with the federal government and 49 states.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The settlement, known as the National Mortgage Settlement (NMS), required the servicers to provide about $26 billion in relief to distressed homeowners and in direct payments to the states and federal government. This settlement amount makes the NMS the second largest civil settlement in U.S. history, only trailing the <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_Master_Settlement_Agreement" title="Tobacco Master Settlement Agreement">Tobacco Master Settlement Agreement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The five banks were also required to comply with 305 new mortgage servicing standards. Oklahoma held out and agreed to settle with the banks separately.
</p><p>On October 24, 2012, American <a href="/wiki/Federal_prosecutor" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal prosecutor">federal prosecutors</a> filed a $1 billion <a href="/wiki/Civil_lawsuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil lawsuit">civil lawsuit</a> against Bank of America for <a href="/wiki/Mortgage_fraud" title="Mortgage fraud">mortgage fraud</a> under the <a href="/wiki/False_Claims_Act" title="False Claims Act">False Claims Act</a>, which provides for possible penalties of triple the damages suffered. The government asserted that <a href="/wiki/Countrywide_Financial" class="mw-redirect" title="Countrywide Financial">Countrywide</a>, which was acquired by Bank of America, <a href="/wiki/Rubber_stamp_(politics)" title="Rubber stamp (politics)">rubber-stamped</a> mortgage loans to risky borrowers and forced taxpayers to guarantee billions of bad loans through <a href="/wiki/Fannie_Mae" title="Fannie Mae">Fannie Mae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mac" title="Freddie Mac">Freddie Mac</a>. The suit was filed by <a href="/wiki/Preet_Bharara" title="Preet Bharara">Preet Bharara</a>, the United States attorney in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, the inspector general of <a href="/wiki/FHFA" class="mw-redirect" title="FHFA">FHFA</a> and the special inspector for the <a href="/wiki/Troubled_Asset_Relief_Program" title="Troubled Asset Relief Program">Troubled Asset Relief Program</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> In March 2014, Bank of America settled the suit by agreeing to pay $6.3 billion to Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac and to buy back around $3.2 billion worth of mortgage bonds.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2014, the Consumer Financial Protection Bureau (CFPB) ordered Bank of America to provide and estimated $727 million in relief to consumers harmed by practices related to credit card add-on products. According to the Bureau, roughly 1.4 million customers were affected by deceptive marketing of add-on products and 1.9 million customers were illegally charged for credit monitoring and reporting services they were not receiving. The deceptive marketing misconduct involved telemarketing scripts containing misstatements and off-script sales pitches made by telemarketers that were misleading and omitted pertinent information. The unfair billing practices involved billing customers for privacy related products without having the authorization necessary to perform the credit monitoring and credit report retrieval services. As a result, the company billed customers for services they did not receive, unfairly charged consumers for interest and fees, illegally charged approximately 1.9 million accounts, and failed to provide the product benefit.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p><p>A $7.5 million settlement was reached in April 2014 with former chief financial officer for Bank of America, Joe L. Price, over allegations that the bank's management withheld material information related to its 2008 merger with <a href="/wiki/Merrill_Lynch" class="mw-redirect" title="Merrill Lynch">Merrill Lynch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> In August 2014, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> and the bank agreed to a $16.65 billion agreement over the sale of risky, mortgage-backed securities before the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>; the loans behind the securities were transferred to the company when it acquired banks such as Merrill Lynch and Countrywide in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-LA_Times_2014_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times_2014-129">[129]</a></sup> As a whole, the three firms provided $965 billion of mortgage-backed securities from 2004–2008.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The settlement was structured to give $7 billion in consumer relief and $9.65 billion in penalty payments to the federal government and state governments; <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, for instance, received $300 million to recompense public pension funds.<sup id="cite_ref-LA_Times_2014_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times_2014-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> The settlement was the largest in United States history between a single company and the federal government.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p><p>In 2018, former senior executive Omeed Malik filed a $100 million <a href="/wiki/Arbitration" title="Arbitration">arbitration</a> case through <a href="/wiki/Financial_Industry_Regulatory_Authority" title="Financial Industry Regulatory Authority">FINRA</a> against Bank of America after the company investigated him for alleged <a href="/wiki/Sexual_misconduct" title="Sexual misconduct">sexual misconduct</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> His <a href="/wiki/Defamation" title="Defamation">defamation</a> claim was on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Workplace_retaliation" class="mw-redirect" title="Workplace retaliation">retaliation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breach_of_contract" title="Breach of contract">breach of contract</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Discrimination" title="Discrimination">discrimination</a> against his <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> background.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Malik received an eight-figure <a href="/wiki/Settlement_(litigation)" title="Settlement (litigation)">settlement</a> in July.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Controversies" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Parmalat_controversy">Parmalat controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Parmalat controversy" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Parmalat" title="Parmalat">Parmalat</a> SpA is a multinational Italian dairy and food corporation. Following <a href="/wiki/Parmalat_bankruptcy_timeline" title="Parmalat bankruptcy timeline">Parmalat's 2003 bankruptcy</a>, the company sued Bank of America for $10 billion, alleging the bank profited from its knowledge of Parmalat's financial difficulties. The parties announced a settlement in July 2009, resulting in Bank of America paying Parmalat $98.5 million in October 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> In a related case, on April 18, 2011, an Italian court acquitted Bank of America and three other large banks, along with their employees, of charges they assisted Parmalat in concealing its fraud, and of lacking sufficient internal controls to prevent such frauds. Prosecutors did not immediately say whether they would appeal the rulings. In <a href="/wiki/Parma" title="Parma">Parma</a>, the banks were still charged with covering up the fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumer_credit_controversies">Consumer credit controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Consumer credit controversies" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In January 2008, Bank of America began notifying some customers without payment problems that their interest rates were more than doubled, up to 28%. The bank was criticized for raising rates on customers in good standing, and for declining to explain why it had done so.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> In September 2009, a Bank of America credit card customer, Ann Minch, posted a video on YouTube criticizing the bank for raising her interest rate. After the video went <a href="/wiki/Viral_video" title="Viral video">viral</a>, she was contacted by a Bank of America representative who lowered her rate. The story attracted national attention from television and internet commentators.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> More recently, the bank has been criticized for allegedly seizing three properties that were not under their ownership, apparently due to incorrect addresses on their legal documents.<sup id="cite_ref-wronghomes_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wronghomes-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: WikiLeaks" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In October 2009, <a href="/wiki/Julian_Assange" title="Julian Assange">Julian Assange</a> of <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a> claimed that his organization possessed a 5 gigabyte <a href="/wiki/Hard_drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Hard drive">hard drive</a> formerly used by a Bank of America executive and that Wikileaks intended to publish its contents.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> published an interview with Assange in which he stated his intent to publish information which would turn a major U.S. bank "inside out".<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> In response to this announcement, Bank of America stock dropped 3.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2010, Bank of America announced that it would no longer service requests to transfer funds to WikiLeaks,<sup id="cite_ref-CB1_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CB1-150">[150]</a></sup> stating that "Bank of America joins in the actions previously announced by <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" class="mw-redirect" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a>, <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a> Europe and others and will not process transactions of any type that we have reason to believe are intended for WikiLeaks... This decision is based upon our reasonable belief that WikiLeaks may be engaged in activities that are, among other things, inconsistent with our internal policies for processing payments."<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p><p>Later in December, it was announced that Bank of America purchased more than 300 <a href="/wiki/Internet_domain_name" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet domain name">Internet domain names</a> in an attempt to preempt bad publicity that might be forthcoming in the anticipated WikiLeaks release. The domain names included as <i>BrianMoynihanBlows.com</i>, <i>BrianMoynihanSucks.com</i> and similar names for other top executives of the bank.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p><p>Sometime before August 2011, WikiLeaks claimed that 5 GB of Bank of America leaks was part of the deletion of over 3500 communications by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Domscheit-Berg" title="Daniel Domscheit-Berg">Daniel Domscheit-Berg</a>, a now ex-WikiLeaks volunteer.<sup id="cite_ref-twitter_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twitter-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-twitterboa_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twitterboa-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Anonymous">Anonymous</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Anonymous" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On March 14, 2011, members of hacker group <a href="/wiki/Anonymous_(group)" title="Anonymous (group)">Anonymous</a> began releasing emails said to be from a former Bank of America employee. According to the group, the emails documented alleged "corruption and fraud". The source, identified publicly as Brian Penny,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> was a former LPI Specialist from Balboa Insurance, a firm which used to be owned by the bank, but was sold to Australian Reinsurance Company QBE.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Mortgage_business">Mortgage business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Mortgage business" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2010 the state of <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> launched an investigation into Bank of America for misleading homeowners who sought to modify their <a href="/wiki/Mortgage_loan" title="Mortgage loan">mortgage loans</a>. According to the attorney general of Arizona, the bank "repeatedly has deceived" such mortgagors. In response to the investigation, the bank has given some modifications on the condition that the homeowners remove some information criticizing the bank online.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Investment_in_mountaintop_removal">Investment in mountaintop removal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Investment in mountaintop removal" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On May 6, 2015, Bank of America announced it would reduce its financial exposure to coal companies. The announcement came following pressure from universities and environmental groups. The new policy was announced as part of the bank's decision to continue to reduce credit exposure over time to the coal mining sector.<sup id="cite_ref-Business_Insider_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Business_Insider-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Competition" data-section="37" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<p>Bank of America's major competitors are <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santander_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander Group">Santander</a>, <a href="/wiki/PNC_Financial_Services" title="PNC Financial Services">PNC Financial Services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ally_Financial" title="Ally Financial">Ally Financial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_One" title="Capital One">Capital One</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chase_Bank" title="Chase Bank">Chase Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/US_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="US Bank">US Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citizens_Financial_Group" title="Citizens Financial Group">Citizens Financial Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%26T_Bank" title="M&amp;T Bank">M&amp;T Bank</a>.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_buildings">Notable buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notable buildings" data-section="38" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_America_Atlanta_1.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bank_of_America_Atlanta_1.jpg/170px-Bank_of_America_Atlanta_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 227px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bank_of_America_Atlanta_1.jpg/170px-Bank_of_America_Atlanta_1.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="227" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_America_Atlanta_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Plaza_(Atlanta)" title="Bank of America Plaza (Atlanta)">Bank of America Plaza</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> is the tallest building in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern United States</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_America_Stadium.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Bank_of_America_Stadium.jpg/220px-Bank_of_America_Stadium.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2229" data-file-height="1430"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 141px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Bank_of_America_Stadium.jpg/220px-Bank_of_America_Stadium.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="141" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_America_Stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Stadium" title="Bank of America Stadium">Bank of America Stadium</a>, home to the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/NFL" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL">NFL</a></div></div></div>
<p>Notable buildings which Bank of America currently occupies include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Tower_(Phoenix)" title="Bank of America Tower (Phoenix)">Bank of America Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Center_(Los_Angeles)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of America Center (Los Angeles)">Bank of America Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles, California">Los Angeles, California</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Transamerica_Pyramid" title="Transamerica Pyramid">Transamerica Pyramid</a>, in San Francisco</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/555_California_Street" title="555 California Street">555 California Street</a>, formerly the Bank of America Center and world headquarters, in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francisco, California">San Francisco, California</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Plaza_(Fort_Lauderdale)" title="Bank of America Plaza (Fort Lauderdale)">Bank of America Plaza</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">Fort Lauderdale, Florida</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Tower_(Jacksonville)" title="Bank of America Tower (Jacksonville)">Bank of America Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville, Florida</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/701_Brickell_Avenue" title="701 Brickell Avenue">Bank of America Financial Center</a> (<a href="/wiki/Brickell" title="Brickell">Brickell</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Museum_Tower_(Miami)" title="Museum Tower (Miami)">Bank of America Museum Tower</a> (<a href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" class="mw-redirect" title="Downtown Miami">Downtown Miami</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" class="mw-redirect" title="Miami, Florida">Miami, Florida</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Center_(Orlando)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of America Center (Orlando)">Bank of America Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Tower_(Saint_Petersburg)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of America Tower (Saint Petersburg)">Bank of America Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Florida" title="St. Petersburg, Florida">St. Petersburg, Florida</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Plaza_(Tampa)" title="Bank of America Plaza (Tampa)">Bank of America Plaza</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa, Florida</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Plaza_(Atlanta)" title="Bank of America Plaza (Atlanta)">Bank of America Plaza</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, Georgia</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LaSalle_National_Bank_Building" class="mw-redirect" title="LaSalle National Bank Building">Bank of America Building</a>, formerly the LaSalle Bank Building in Chicago, Illinois</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/One_City_Center_(Portland)" title="One City Center (Portland)">One City Center</a>, often called the Bank of America building due to signage rights, in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Maine" title="Portland, Maine">Portland, Maine</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Building_(Baltimore)" title="Bank of America Building (Baltimore)">Bank of America Building</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, Maryland</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Plaza_(St._Louis)" title="Bank of America Plaza (St. Louis)">Bank of America Plaza</a> in <a href="/wiki/St_Louis,_Missouri" class="mw-redirect" title="St Louis, Missouri">St Louis, Missouri</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Tower_(Albuquerque)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of America Tower (Albuquerque)">Bank of America Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque,_New_Mexico" title="Albuquerque, New Mexico">Albuquerque, New Mexico</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Tower_(New_York_City)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of America Tower (New York City)">Bank of America Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Corporate_Center" title="Bank of America Corporate Center">Bank of America Corporate Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a> (the corporate headquarters)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Plaza_(Charlotte)" title="Bank of America Plaza (Charlotte)">Bank of America Plaza</a> in Charlotte, North Carolina</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Legacy_Union_(development)" title="Legacy Union (development)">Bank of America Tower</a> in Charlotte, North Carolina</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hearst_Tower_(Charlotte)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hearst Tower (Charlotte)">Hearst Tower</a> in Charlotte, North Carolina</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Plaza_(Dallas)" title="Bank of America Plaza (Dallas)">Bank of America Plaza</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>, Texas</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Center_(Houston)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of America Center (Houston)">Bank of America Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, Texas</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Building_(Midland)" title="Bank of America Building (Midland)">Bank of America Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Midland,_Texas" title="Midland, Texas">Midland, Texas</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Plaza_(San_Antonio)" title="Bank of America Plaza (San Antonio)">Bank of America Plaza</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio" title="San Antonio">San Antonio</a>, Texas</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Fifth_Avenue_Plaza" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of America Fifth Avenue Plaza">Bank of America Fifth Avenue Plaza</a> in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, Washington</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Columbia_Center" title="Columbia Center">Columbia Center</a> in Seattle, Washington</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Tower_(Hong_Kong)" title="Bank of America Tower (Hong Kong)">Bank of America Tower</a> in Hong Kong</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/City_Place_I" title="City Place I">City Place I</a>, also known as United Healthcare Center, in <a href="/wiki/Hartford,_Connecticut" title="Hartford, Connecticut">Hartford, Connecticut</a> (the tallest building in Connecticut)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/9454_Wilshire_Boulevard" title="9454 Wilshire Boulevard">9454 Wilshire Boulevard</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Hills,_California" title="Beverly Hills, California">Beverly Hills, California</a></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_buildings">Former buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bank_of_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Former buildings" data-section="39" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Robert_B._Atwood_Building" title="Robert B. Atwood Building">Robert B. Atwood Building</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anchorage,_Alaska" title="Anchorage, Alaska">Anchorage, Alaska</a> was at one time named the Bank of America Center, renamed in conjunction with the bank's acquisition of building tenant Security Pacific Bank. This particular branch was later acquired by Alaska-based Northrim Bank and moved across the street to the <a href="/wiki/Linny_Pacillo_Parking_Garage" title="Linny Pacillo Parking Garage">Linny Pacillo Parking Garage</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Building_(Providence)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of America Building (Providence)">Bank of America Building (Providence)</a> opened in 1928 as the Industrial Trust Building and remains the tallest building in Rhode Island. Through a number of mergers it was later known as the Industrial National Bank building and the Fleet Bank building. The building was leased by Bank of America from 2004 to 2012 and has been vacant since March 2013. The building is commonly known as the Superman Building based on a popular belief that it was the model for the <a href="/wiki/Daily_Planet" title="Daily Planet">Daily Planet</a> building in the <a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">Superman</a> comic books.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Miami_Tower" title="Miami Tower">Miami Tower</a> iconic in its appearance in <i><a href="/wiki/Miami_Vice" title="Miami Vice">Miami Vice</a></i> was known as the Bank of America Tower for many years. It is located in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" class="mw-redirect" title="Downtown Miami">Downtown Miami</a>. On April 18, 2012, the AIA's Florida Chapter placed it on its list of Florida Architecture: 100 Years. 100 Places as the Bank of America Tower.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
<cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071103060809/http://www.visalatam.com/e_aboutvisa/acerca_historia.jsp">"The History of Visa"</a>. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">October 29,</span> 2007</span>. <q>Bank of America had the entire state of California as a potential market, and when it issued BankAmericard in 1958, the card was an instant success. [...] In many countries, there was still reluctance to issue a card associated with Bank of America, even though the association was entirely nominal in nature. For this reason, in 1977 BankAmericard became the Visa card, retaining its distinctive blue, white and gold flag. NBI became Visa U.S.A., and IBANCO became Visa International.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=The+History+of+Visa&amp;rft.pub=Visa+Inc.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.visalatam.com%2Fe_aboutvisa%2Facerca_historia.jsp&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABank+of+America" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
